width="25" height="25" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/PR_primary_52.svg/38px-PR_primary_52.svg.png 1.5x, scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.Caguas.gov.pr">caguas.gov.pr</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Caguas</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;\xcb\x88ka\xc9\xa3was&#93;</a></span>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1177148991"><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">locally</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">&#91;\xcb\x88kawa\xca\x94&#93;</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Caguas_barrio-pueblo" title="Caguas barrio-pueblo">city</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Central Mountain Range of Puerto Rico</a>, south of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Trujillo Alto</a>, west of <a href="/wiki/Gurabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gurabo, Puerto Rico">Gurabo</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Lorenzo, Puerto Rico">San Lorenzo</a>, and east of <a href="/wiki/Aguas_Buenas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguas Buenas, Puerto Rico">Aguas Buenas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cidra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cidra, Puerto Rico">Cidra</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cayey, Puerto Rico">Cayey</a>. Caguas was founded in 1775. The municipality had a population of 127,244 at the <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_census" title="2020 United States census">2020 census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Caguas is located 20 miles (32&#160;km) from <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>. It is located in the <i>Valle de Caguas</i> or <a href="/wiki/Caguas_Valley" title="Caguas Valley">Caguas Valley</a> (also known as <i>Valle del Turabo</i> or the Turabo Valley), at the eastern ranges of the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Central Mountain Range</a>. It is known as <i>La Ciudad Criolla</i> (<a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">Criollo</a> City), <i>Valle del Turabo</i> (the <a href="/wiki/Turabo_River" title="Turabo River">Turabo</a> Valley) and <i>La Cuna de los Trovadores</i> (The Cradle of the <i>Trovadores</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its name originates from the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacique</a> <a href="/wiki/Caguax" title="Caguax">Caguax</a>, who was a regional chief. Caguas is a principal city of both the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area">San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Carolina,_PR_Combined_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan-Carolina, PR Combined Statistical Area">San Juan-Caguas-Fajardo Combined Statistical Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-enciclop_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enciclop-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2009 Caguas is the only municipality in Puerto Rico recognized as a <a href="/wiki/Tree_City_USA" class="mw-redirect" title="Tree City USA">Tree City USA</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Arbor_Day_Foundation" title="Arbor Day Foundation">Arbor Day Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><p>\nThe area of the <a href="/wiki/Caguas_Valley" title="Caguas Valley">Valley of Caguas</a> was first settled by the <a href="/wiki/Saladoid" title="Saladoid">Saladoid culture</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawak</a> culture which originated in northern South America (today <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>), approximately between the years 100 BCE to 600 CE. Findings from the Cag\xc3\xbcitas archaeological site (CS-2) indicate that the area was later inhabited by various pre-<a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> (Ostionoid) cultures which first developed agriculture in the valley, primarily the cultivation of <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, and hunted now extinct species such as <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_hutia" title="Puerto Rican hutia">hutias</a>. As with the rest of Puerto Rico, the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadnos</a> were the primary group living in the valley at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish arrival</a>. The Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistadors</a> further developed the agriculture in the valley, while also establishing mines in search of <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">silver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>. Most of the native Ta\xc3\xadnos living in the area were either forced out or taken as slaves and moved to the Real Hacienda del Toa (in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Toa_Alta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Alta, Puerto Rico">Toa Alta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a>). Most of the valley was later cleared of its original vegetation for the development of cattle farms such as <i>Hato de Bairoa</i>, <i>Hato de Caguax</i> and <i>Hato de Gurabo</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p><figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Caguas_-_Typical_scene.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Caguas_-_Typical_scene.jpg/220px-Caguas_-_Typical_scene.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Caguas_-_Typical_scene.jpg/330px-Caguas_-_Typical_scene.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Caguas_-_Typical_scene.jpg/440px-Caguas_-_Typical_scene.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1615" data-file-height="1042" /></a><figcaption>Postcard from 1912 showing a typical street in Caguas at the beginning of the 20th century.</figcaption></figure><p>Caguas was officially founded on January 1, 1775, as <b>San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n del Pi\xc3\xb1al de Caguax</b>, with the name later being shortened and modernized to its current form. The name of the city comes from <a href="/wiki/Caguax" title="Caguax">Caguax</a>, a local <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> chief and early convert to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>. The site of the historic <a href="/wiki/Caguas_barrio-pueblo" title="Caguas barrio-pueblo">downtown</a> area of Caguas and its central square dates to 1779. In 1820 the settlement was granted the title of <i>Villa</i> and it was granted city rights in 1894. <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">Sugarcane</a> was the primary crop during this time and important sugarcane plantations and refineries were those of Central Santa Juana (close to modern day <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Centro_Mall" title="Plaza Centro Mall">Plaza Centro</a>) and Central Santa Catalina (modern day <a href="/wiki/Las_Catalinas_Mall" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Catalinas Mall">Las Catalinas Mall</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Carretera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Carretera Central (Puerto Rico)">Carretera Central</a>, which is the first paved road to cross Puerto Rico from north to south connecting <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>, was built during the last two decades of the 19th century,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> made Caguas more accessible therefore causing the population of the town to grow even more.\n</p><p>Puerto Rico was ceded by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> and became a territory of the United States. In 1899, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">United States Department of War</a> conducted a <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Caguas was 19,857.<sup id="cite_ref-OfficeSanger1900_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OfficeSanger1900-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The city grew considerably in size during the 1970s<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and quickly became an <a href="/wiki/Exurb" title="Exurb">exurb</a> of San Juan to the north due to its location. The region of Caguas became an important <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharmaceuticals industry">pharmaceuticals</a> manufacturing center during this time. Pharmaceutical companies originally came to Puerto Rico in the late 1960s and 1970s to take advantage of the now-expired federal tax incentive known as <i>Section 936</i>. This incentive allowed U.S.-based manufacturers to send all profits from local plants to stateside parent plants without having to pay any federal taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Although not typically seen as part of the colloquial <i>\xc3\x81rea Metro</i> of San Juan (<a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>), the municipality of Caguas is located in the census-based <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan metropolitan area">San Juan Metropolitan Area</a> due to its role as a <a href="/wiki/Commuter_town" title="Commuter town">commuter town</a>. The average commute time for residents of the municipality is 30.5 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-Caguas,_PR_&#123;&#123;!&#125;&#125;_Data_USA_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caguas,_PR_{{!}}_Data_USA-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Caguas is the fourth most populous city in the San Juan Metropolitan region and the most populous city in Puerto Rico that is not located in a coastal area.\n</p><p>On August 7, 2002, Caguas was the site of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_accidents_and_incidents_involving_military_aircraft_(2000%E2%80%932009)" title="List of accidents and incidents involving military aircraft (2000\xe2\x80\x932009)">2002 USAF Hercules air disaster</a>, where all 10 military personnel on board lost their lives after an airplane carrying them struck a mountain in the south of the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> on September 20, 2017, triggered numerous landslides in Caguas with its wind and rain. Rivers were breached causing flooding of low-lying areas, and infrastructure and homes were destroyed. The hurricane caused $90 million in damages in Caguas.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ENDI_Maria_2019_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENDI_Maria_2019-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> More specifically, 40 homes were left without a roof and 30 were flooded in the Morales neighborhood. <i>Escuela Segunda Unidad Diego V\xc3\xa1zquez</i> and the <i>Centro Multiusos</i> flooded as well.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:2022viewofcaguas1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/2022viewofcaguas1.jpg/220px-2022viewofcaguas1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/2022viewofcaguas1.jpg/330px-2022viewofcaguas1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/2022viewofcaguas1.jpg/440px-2022viewofcaguas1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Caguas from the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Cayey" title="Sierra de Cayey">Sierra de Cayey</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The city and municipality of Caguas are located approximately 30 minutes from the coastline both on the east (<a href="/wiki/Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Humacao, Puerto Rico">Humacao</a>) and the north (<a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>). It is east of <a href="/wiki/Aguas_Buenas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguas Buenas, Puerto Rico">Aguas Buenas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cidra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cidra, Puerto Rico">Cidra</a>, north of <a href="/wiki/Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cayey, Puerto Rico">Cayey</a>, south of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, and west of <a href="/wiki/Gurabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gurabo, Puerto Rico">Gurabo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Trujillo Alto</a>. It also shares borders with <a href="/wiki/Guayama,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guayama, Puerto Rico">Guayama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patillas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Patillas, Puerto Rico">Patillas</a> via a five-point border at the summit of <a href="/wiki/Cerro_La_Santa" title="Cerro La Santa">Cerro La Santa</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cayey, Puerto Rico">Cayey</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Lorenzo, Puerto Rico">San Lorenzo</a>. This is the tallest point of the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Cayey" title="Sierra de Cayey">Sierra de Cayey</a>, not to be confused with Monta\xc3\xb1a Santa (officially called Cerro de Nuestra Madre) which is another mountain in the same massif located on the boundary between the municipalities of Patillas and San Lorenzo. At this point there are two tall antennas which provide signal to Puerto Rico\'s principal TV stations such as <a href="/wiki/WKAQ-TV" title="WKAQ-TV">WKAQ-TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/WAPA-TV" title="WAPA-TV">WAPA-TV</a>. No road passes exactly at this point, and it can be approached nearby through <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_184" title="Puerto Rico Highway 184">Puerto Rico Highway 184</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Valle_de_Caguas">Valle de Caguas</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Valle de Caguas"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Caguas_Valley" title="Caguas Valley">Caguas Valley</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_del_area_de_Caguas_desde_el_cerro_las_pi%C3%B1as_-_panoramio.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Vista_del_area_de_Caguas_desde_el_cerro_las_pi%C3%B1as_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Vista_del_area_de_Caguas_desde_el_cerro_las_pi%C3%B1as_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Vista_del_area_de_Caguas_desde_el_cerro_las_pi%C3%B1as_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Vista_del_area_de_Caguas_desde_el_cerro_las_pi%C3%B1as_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Vista_del_area_de_Caguas_desde_el_cerro_las_pi%C3%B1as_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Vista_del_area_de_Caguas_desde_el_cerro_las_pi%C3%B1as_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption>View of the Caguas Valley from Cerro Las Pi\xc3\xb1as in <a href="/wiki/Beatriz,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Beatriz, Cayey, Puerto Rico">Beatriz, Cayey</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The city is located in one of the largest valleys in Puerto Rico, the <i>Valle de Caguas</i> or <b><a href="/wiki/Caguas_Valley" title="Caguas Valley">Caguas Valley</a></b> (also known as <i>Valle del Turabo</i> or the <a href="/wiki/Turabo_River" title="Turabo River">Turabo</a> Valley).<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Being located in a valley, Caguas has the distinction of being relatively flat except near the borders with all the mentioned municipalities except Gurabo.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The valley is bordered by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Altos_de_La_Mesa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Altos de La Mesa (page does not exist)">Altos de La Mesa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Altos_de_San_Luis" title="Altos de San Luis">San Luis</a> ranges in the north, the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Luquillo" title="Sierra de Luquillo">Sierra de Luquillo</a> on the northeast, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Lorenzo_batholith&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Lorenzo batholith (page does not exist)">San Lorenzo batholith</a> to the east, the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Cayey" title="Sierra de Cayey">Sierra de Cayey</a> on the south and the main range of the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a> to the west.\n</p><p>This valley is fed mainly by the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Lo%C3%ADza" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza">Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza River</a>, one of Puerto Rico\'s major rivers that feed into the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, and numerous tributaries such as the <a href="/wiki/Cag%C3%BCitas_River" title="Cag\xc3\xbcitas River">Cag\xc3\xbcitas</a>, along which the contemporary settlement of <a href="/wiki/Caguas_barrio-pueblo" title="Caguas barrio-pueblo">Caguas</a> was built. The city\'s nickname <i>Valle del Turabo</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Turabo_River" title="Turabo River">Turabo River</a>, which is another tributary that flows from the south. The <a href="/wiki/Gurabo_River" title="Gurabo River">Gurabo River</a>, another major tributary, feeds into the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Lo%C3%ADza" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza">Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza</a> at a region where the valley narrows into a <a href="/wiki/Rift_valley" title="Rift valley">rift valley</a> that runs from west to east and ends in <a href="/wiki/Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Humacao, Puerto Rico">Humacao</a> in the southeastern coast of the island.\n</p><p>As with other parts of Puerto Rico, the region of Caguas is susceptible to earthquakes. The municipality is located along the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Northern_Puerto_Rico_fault_zone&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Great Northern Puerto Rico fault zone (page does not exist)">Great Northern Puerto Rico fault zone</a> (GNPRfz) and in recent times the region experienced moderate size earthquakes in 1990<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/2010_Aguas_Buenas_earthquake" title="2010 Aguas Buenas earthquake">2010</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Water_features">Water features</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Water features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Lo%C3%ADza" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza">R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza</a> divides the municipality from <a href="/wiki/Gurabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gurabo, Puerto Rico">Gurabo</a>.</li>\n<li>Other rivers: <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Turabo" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Turabo">R\xc3\xado Turabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cag%C3%BCitas_River" title="Cag\xc3\xbcitas River">R\xc3\xado Cag\xc3\xbcitas</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Ca%C3%B1aboncito" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Ca\xc3\xb1aboncito">R\xc3\xado Ca\xc3\xb1aboncito</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Bairoa" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Bairoa">R\xc3\xado Bairoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Ca%C3%B1as_(Caguas,_Puerto_Rico)" title="R\xc3\xado Ca\xc3\xb1as (Caguas, Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado Ca\xc3\xb1as</a>.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Restoring_the_electrical_grid_in_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico,_post_Hurricane_Maria.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Restoring_the_electrical_grid_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_post_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/220px-Restoring_the_electrical_grid_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_post_Hurricane_Maria.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Restoring_the_electrical_grid_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_post_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/330px-Restoring_the_electrical_grid_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_post_Hurricane_Maria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Restoring_the_electrical_grid_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_post_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/440px-Restoring_the_electrical_grid_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_post_Hurricane_Maria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a><figcaption>Restoring the electrical grid in Caguas, post Hurricane Maria.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The climate is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon climate</a>, meaning the daily mean temperature from month to month is never less than 64.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F (18.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C), and there is a distinct wet and dry season. Rainfall is common in relative abundance throughout most of the year, although there is less rain than in the eastern coastal valleys. The land, however, is fertile and deep.\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:auto; text-align:center; line-height:1.2em;">\n<caption>Climate data for Caguas (Average and Records: id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Caguas,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/220px-Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" /></a><figcaption>Subdivisions of Caguas.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Caguas is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 30em;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Caguas_barrio-pueblo" title="Caguas Rico">R\xc3\xado Ca\xc3\xb1as</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/San_Antonio,_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Antonio, Caguas, Puerto Rico">San Antonio</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/San_Salvador,_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Salvador, Caguas, Puerto Rico">San Salvador</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_de_Castro,_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Tom\xc3\xa1s de Castro, Caguas, Puerto Rico">Tom\xc3\xa1s de Castro</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Turabo,_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Turabo, Caguas, Puerto Rico">Turabo</a></li></ol>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are, in contemporary times, roughly comparable to  <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and subbarrios,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_000_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map_000-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_001_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map_001-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_002_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map_002-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span> (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Caguas: Bairoa La 25, Morales neighborhood, Parcelas Viejas in Borinqu\xc3\xa9n, Sector La Barra, and Comunidad La Quebrada in R\xc3\xado Ca\xc3\xb1as, Hoyo Fr\xc3\xado in Las Carolinas, Lajitas, Las Carolinas, Los Muchos, Los Panes in Beatriz, and Savarona.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wordpress.com_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordpress.com-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:PlazaPalmer1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/PlazaPalmer1.jpg/220px-PlazaPalmer1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/PlazaPalmer1.jpg/330px-PlazaPalmer1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/PlazaPalmer1.jpg/440px-PlazaPalmer1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="640" /></a><figcaption>Plaza Palmer, <a href="/wiki/Caguas_barrio-pueblo" title="Caguas barrio-pueblo">Caguas</a>\'s main town square, during <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a>.</figcaption></figure><p>There are seven places in Caguas listed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">US National Register of Historic Places</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-NRHP_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRHP-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Caguas_City_Hall" title="Caguas City Hall">Caguas City Hall</a> (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Alcaldia de Caguas</i></span>, the city hall building)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Primera_Iglesia_Bautista_de_Caguas" title="Primera Iglesia Bautista de Caguas">Primera Iglesia Bautista de Caguas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gautier_Ben%C3%ADtez_High_School" title="Gautier Ben\xc3\xadtez High School">Gautier Ben\xc3\xadtez High School</a></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Escuela Vocacional Aguayo Aldea</i></span></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Logia Union y Amparo #44</i></span></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puente_No._6" title="Puente No. 6">Puente No. 6</a> or (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Puente La Concepci\xc3\xb3n</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carretera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Carretera Central (Puerto Rico)">Carretera Central</a></li></ul>\n<p>Other landscapes, landmarks and tourist attractions in Caguas include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Caguas_Museum_of_Art" title="Caguas Museum of Art">Caguas Museum of Art</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Caguas_Museum_of_Folk_Arts" title="Caguas Museum of Folk Arts">Caguas Museum of Folk Arts</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Caguas_City_Hall" title="Caguas City Hall">Caguas Museum of History</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Herminio_Torres_Grillo_Tobacco_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Herminio Torres Grillo Tobacco Museum (page does not exist)">Caguas Tobacco Museum</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Catedral_Dulce_Nombre_de_Jes%C3%BAs_(Caguas,_Puerto_Rico)" title="Catedral Dulce Nombre de Jes\xc3\xbas (Caguas, Puerto Rico)">Dulce Nombre de Jes\xc3\xbas Cathedral</a> (Catedral de Caguas), the <a href="/wiki/Caguas_City_Hall" title="Caguas City Hall">old city hall</a> and other historical buildings at Plaza Palmer, the main town square.</li>\n<li>Hacienda Catalina Ruins, located in the area of <a href="/wiki/Las_Catalinas_Mall" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Catalinas Mall">Las Catalinas Mall</a></li>\n<li>Hacienda Country Club</li>\n<li>La Casa del Ajedrez (The House of <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">Chess</a>)</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Parks_and_natural_areas">Parks and natural areas</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Parks and natural areas"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Jard%C3%ADn_Bot%C3%A1nico_Caguas.tiff" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Jard%C3%ADn_Bot%C3%A1nico_Caguas.tiff/lossy-page1-300px-Jard%C3%ADn_Bot%C3%A1nico_Caguas.tiff.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="201" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Jard%C3%ADn_Bot%C3%A1nico_Caguas.tiff/lossy-page1-450px-Jard%C3%ADn_Bot%C3%A1nico_Caguas.tiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Jard%C3%ADn_Bot%C3%A1nico_Caguas.tiff/lossy-page1-600px-Jard%C3%ADn_Bot%C3%A1nico_Caguas.tiff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>Lotus flower in the Jard\xc3\xadn Bot\xc3\xa1nico y Cultural William Miranda Mar\xc3\xadn</figcaption></figure><p>The municipality of Caguas is home to various parks and natural protected areas managed by different governmental entities ranging from the municipal government, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Natural_and_Environmental_Resources" title="Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources">Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Conservation_Trust_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Conservation Trust of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico Conservation Trust</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service" title="United States Fish and Wildlife Service">United States Fish &amp; Wildlife Service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aguas_Buenas_Cave_System" title="Aguas Buenas Cave System">Aguas Buenas Cave and Caverns System Nature Reserve</a>, an extensive cave system partially located in the municipality of Caguas.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bairoa_River" title="Bairoa River">Bairoa River Natural Protected Area</a>, protected <a href="/wiki/Riparian_forest" title="Riparian forest">riparian forest</a> along the Bairoa River.</li>\n<li>Borinquen Valley Natural Area, 25 acres of protected forest located in barrio <a href="/wiki/Borinquen,_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Borinquen, Caguas, Puerto Rico">Borinquen</a>.</li>\n<li>Caguas Real Nature Reserve, 60 acres of riparian forest along the <a href="/wiki/Turabo_River" title="Turabo River">Turabo River</a> managed by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service" title="United States Fish and Wildlife Service">United States Fish &amp; Wildlife Service</a>.</li>\n<li>Caguas Regional Forest, a protected <a href="/wiki/Secondary_forest" title="Secondary forest">secondary forest</a> and riparian ecosystem along the Turabo River.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carite_State_Forest" title="Carite State Forest">Carite State Forest and Reserve</a>, one of the 20 units in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Puerto_Rico_state_forests" title="List of Puerto Rico state forests">state forest system of Puerto Rico</a>, partially located in Caguas.</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cerro_Borr%C3%A1s&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cerro Borr\xc3\xa1s (page does not exist)">Cerro Borr\xc3\xa1s</a>, formerly home to various recreational parks such as Moisty Park, currently preserved as a secondary forest.</li>\n<li>Chalets de Bairoa Natural Area, currently being developed as a preserved ecological corridor within the Valley of Caguas.</li>\n<li>Charco El Cantil, natural swimming pool located along the <a href="/wiki/Turabo_River" title="Turabo River">Turabo River</a>.</li>\n<li>Finca Longo and <a href="/wiki/Altos_de_San_Luis" title="Altos de San Luis">Altos de San Luis</a>, partially managed by the DRNA forest service and the municipality of Caguas.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/William_Miranda_Mar%C3%ADn_Botanical_and_Cultural_Garden" title="William Miranda Mar\xc3\xadn Botanical and Cultural Garden">Jard\xc3\xadn Bot\xc3\xa1nico y Cultural William Miranda Mar\xc3\xadn</a> (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071029004228/http://www.caguas.com.pr/Default.aspx?tabid=207">Botanical and Cultural Gardens</a>), botanical garden and cultural institution containing the ruins of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hacienda_San_Jos%C3%A9_de_Caguas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hacienda San Jos\xc3\xa9 de Caguas (page does not exist)">Hacienda San Jos\xc3\xa9</a> plantation and <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> archaeological sites, located in <i>barrio</i> <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ab%C3%B3n,_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ca\xc3\xb1ab\xc3\xb3n, Caguas, Puerto Rico">Ca\xc3\xb1ab\xc3\xb3n</a>.</li>\n<li>Jorge Sotomayor del Toro Protected Natural Area, a <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected areas of Puerto Rico">protected natural area</a> located adjacent to the Carite Forest.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Voy_Turistiendo_Campaign"><i>Voy Turistiendo</i> Campaign</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Voy Turistiendo Campaign"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>To stimulate local tourism during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Puerto_Rico" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Puerto Rico">COVID-19 pandemic in Puerto Rico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a> launched the <i>Voy Turistiendo</i> (I\'m Touring) campaign in 2021. The campaign featured a passport book with a page for each municipality. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Voy Turisteando</i></span> Caguas passport page lists the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Jard\xc3\xadn Bot\xc3\xa1nico William Miranda Marin</i></span>, the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Catedral Dulce Nombre de Jes\xc3\xbas</i></span>, the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Plaza de Recreo Santiago R. Palmer</i></span> and the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Museo de Artes Populares</i></span> as places of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Caguas celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in July. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de Nuestra Sra. del Carmen</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Rosario Cantado a los Reyes</i></span> \xe2\x80\x93 4 January</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071206100328/http://portalesp.caguas.gov.pr/eventos/e_reyes.htm">Three Kings Festival</a> \xe2\x80\x93 5 January</li>\n<li>Criolla Beatriz \xe2\x80\x93 February</li>\n<li>Criolla Borinquen Fair \xe2\x80\x93 March</li>\n<li>Criolla Ca\xc3\xb1ab\xc3\xb3n Fair \xe2\x80\x93 April</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Felipe_%22La_Voz%22_Rodr%C3%ADguez" class="mw-redirect" title="Felipe &quot;La Voz&quot; Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Felipe "La Voz" Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a>\' Birthday \xe2\x80\x93 8 May</li>\n<li>Al Fresco \xe2\x80\x93 Every last Friday of each month</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071206085258/http://portalesp.caguas.gov.pr/eventos/e_fiestascruz.htm">Cross Festival</a> \xe2\x80\x93 23\xe2\x80\x9331 May</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071206074929/http://portalesp.caguas.gov.pr/eventos/e_festivalcriollo.htm">Typical Criole Festival</a> \xe2\x80\x93 1\xe2\x80\x932 June</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071206093648/http://portalesp.caguas.gov.pr/eventos/e_musical.htm">Latin American Musical</a></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Caguas_(baseball_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="Caguas (baseball club)">Criollos de Caguas</a> baseball team is considered one of the greatest of all time in all of Latin America, having won 18 national Puerto Rico titles and 5 <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_World_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean World Series">Caribbean World Series</a> titles The team is a member of the <i>Liga de B\xc3\xa9isbol Profesional de Puerto Rico</i> (<a href="/wiki/Professional_Baseball_League_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Professional Baseball League of Puerto Rico">LBPPR</a>). Three of the first five Puerto Ricans that played Major League Baseball in the U.S. mainland, at one point in their careers played for the Criollos de Caguas (<a href="/wiki/Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Olmo" class="mw-redirect" title="Luis Rodr\xc3\xadguez Olmo">Luis Rodr\xc3\xadguez Olmo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victor_Pellot" class="mw-redirect" title="Victor Pellot">Victor Pellot Power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Clemente" title="Roberto Clemente">Roberto Clemente</a>).\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Caguas_Creoles_(basketball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Caguas Creoles (basketball)">Criollos de Caguas</a> basketball team, founded in 1968 by Dr. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hector_Davila&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hector Davila (page does not exist)">H\xc3\xa9ctor "Tato" D\xc3\xa1vila</a> and Lcdo. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Libertario_P%C3%A9rez_Rodr%C3%ADguez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Libertario P\xc3\xa9rez Rodr\xc3\xadguez (page does not exist)">Libertario P\xc3\xa9rez Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> (a lawyer), is a basketball team that did not enjoy as much success as their baseball counterparts. However, in the early 2000s, they showed a lot of progress by reaching the national playoffs various times. The team was a member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Superior_Basketball_League_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="National Superior Basketball League of Puerto Rico">BSN</a>. In 2006, the team won its first BSN national basketball championship, defeating <a href="/wiki/Flor_Melendez" class="mw-redirect" title="Flor Melendez">Flor Melendez</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Cangrejeros_de_Santurce_(basketball)" title="Cangrejeros de Santurce (basketball)">Santurce Crabbers</a> in five games.\n</p><p>Caguas is home to the <a href="/wiki/Bairoa_Gym" title="Bairoa Gym">Bairoa Gym</a>, one of the most important boxing gyms in all Puerto Rico and a place where many local and visiting champions and otherwise notable boxers have trained at; such as boxing Welterweight Champion <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Cotto" title="Miguel Cotto">Miguel Cotto</a>, his brother <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Cotto" class="mw-redirect" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Cotto">Jose Miguel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Mercado" title="Alberto Mercado">Alberto Mercado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carazo" title="Juan Carazo">Juan Carazo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Escalera" title="Alfredo Escalera">Alfredo Escalera</a> and others.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Criollas_de_Caguas" title="Criollas de Caguas">Criollas de Caguas</a> women\'s volleyball team has won 9 national Puerto Rico titles and has made it to the finals more than 15 times. The team is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Liga_de_Voleibol_Superior_Femenino" title="Liga de Voleibol Superior Femenino">Liga de Voleibol Superior Femenino</a> (LVSF).\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Criollos_de_Caguas_FC" title="Criollos de Caguas FC">Criollos de Caguas FC</a> soccer team is considered one of the most successful clubs in the island winning multiple tournaments and cups in Puerto Rican soccer including the National League Title in 2015.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In September 2005, city mayor <a href="/wiki/William_Miranda_Mar%C3%ADn" title="William Miranda Mar\xc3\xadn">William Miranda Mar\xc3\xadn</a> levied the first municipal tax in Puerto Rico via city ordinance. Area merchants now charge a one cent tax for every dollar spent at all retail businesses. The tax has become known around the island as the "<a href="/wiki/Willie_Tax" title="Willie Tax">Willie Tax</a>." It resulted in an estimated $500,000 monthly income for the city. However, the municipal tax was increased to 1.5% after the establishment of the 5.5% state tax, for a total of 7%, and the tax was declared illegal by the Puerto Rico\'s Supreme Court.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 2006, Miranda Mar\xc3\xadn began calling Caguas "El Nuevo Pa\xc3\xads de Caguas" ("The New Country of Caguas").\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture">Agriculture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Agriculture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>During the early part of the 20th century, Caguas hosted one of Puerto Rico\'s most important sugar manufacturers, which gave employment to thousands of Cag\xc3\xbce\xc3\xb1os.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Business">Business</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Business"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Numerous businesses and important buildings have opened in Caguas since the 1970s, including the imposing 23 story apartment building <a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas_Tower&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Caguas Tower (page does not exist)">Caguas Tower</a>, its adjacent competitors Bonneville Apartments, and the 10 floor <a href="/w/index.php?title=Menonita_Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Menonita Hospital (page does not exist)">Menonita Hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are also several shopping centers:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Plaza_del_Carmen_Mall" title="Plaza del Carmen Mall">Plaza del Carmen Mall</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Plaza_Centro_Mall" title="Plaza Centro Mall">Plaza Centro Mall</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Las_Catalinas_Mall" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Catalinas Mall">Las Catalinas Mall</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Prados_Mall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Los Prados Mall (page does not exist)">Los Prados Mall</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bairoa_Shopping_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bairoa Shopping Center (page does not exist)">Bairoa Shopping Center</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Villa_Blanca_Mall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Villa Blanca Mall (page does not exist)">Villa Blanca Mall</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angora_Shopping_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Angora Shopping Center (page does not exist)">Angora Shopping Center</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaza_Degetau_(Caguas)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Plaza Degetau (Caguas) (page does not exist)">Plaza Degetau</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaza_Caguitas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Plaza Caguitas (page does not exist)">Plaza Caguitas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Del_Rio_Shopping_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Del Rio Shopping Center (page does not exist)">Del Rio Shopping Center</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metro_Plaza_(Caguas,_Puerto_Rico)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Metro Plaza (Caguas, Puerto Rico) (page does not exist)">Metro Plaza (Caguas, Puerto Rico)</a></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n2020<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>In 1899, the United States conducted its first <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Caguas was 19,857.\n</p><p>In 2020, Caguas had a population of 127,244 compared to 142,893 in 2010. This shows an 11% decrease in the population in the municipality. The population density in 2020 was 2,200 people&#160;per square mile (850 people/km<sup>2</sup>). <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States census">Latino</a> of any race constitute 98.4% of the population of the municipality. There are also communities of <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Dominican Republic immigration to Puerto Rico">Dominicans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuban_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Cuban immigration to the United States">Cubans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colombians" title="Colombians">Colombians</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of mayors of Caguas, Puerto Rico">List of mayors of Caguas, Puerto Rico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>All municipalities in Puerto Rico are administered by a <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a>, elected every four years. The mayor of the city of Caguas were\n</p><p>1953 to 1969 - Angel Rivera <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">PPD</a>\n</p><p>1969 to 1973 - Miguel Hernandez Rodriguez (New Progressive Party (PNP))\n</p><p>1973 to 1977 - <a href="/wiki/Angel_O._Berrios" class="mw-redirect" title="Angel O. Berrios">Angel O. Berrios</a> Diaz (PPD)\n</p><p>1977 to 1981 - Miguel Hernandez Rodriguez (PNP)\n</p><p>1981 to 1997 - Angel O. Berrios Diaz (PPD)\n</p><p>1997 to 2010 - <a href="/wiki/William_Miranda_Mar%C3%ADn" title="William Miranda Mar\xc3\xadn">William Miranda Mar\xc3\xadn</a> (PPD)\n</p><p>2010 to present - <a href="/wiki/William_Miranda_Torres" title="William Miranda Torres">William Miranda Torres</a> (PPD)\n</p><p>The city belongs to the Senatorial district VII (Humacao), which is represented by two Senators. In 2016, Miguel Laureano (PNP) and Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Dalmau (PPD) were elected as District Senators.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> or municipality has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag_and_coat_of_arms">Flag and coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Flag and coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The colors <a href="/wiki/Blue" title="Blue">blue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gold_(color)" title="Gold (color)">gold</a> were chosen for the shield, distinctive of the city of Caguas. The figures symbolize both the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> origins of the city.\n</p><p>The coat of arms consists of a shield with a blue field. Upon the field are two sets of three golden arrows, forming a <a href="/wiki/Saltire" title="Saltire">cross of St. Andrew</a>. Above the cross is a crown which represents <a href="/wiki/Caguax" title="Caguax">Caguax</a>, cacique of the Turabo Valley region at the time of the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spanish</a> conquerors. Arrows were used as a remembrance of the first Christian place of worship established in the region which was dedicated under the patronage of <a href="/wiki/St._Sebastian" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Sebastian">St. Sebastian</a>. There are <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">pineapples</a> interspersed to reflect the native agriculture. A <a href="/wiki/Castellation" class="mw-redirect" title="Castellation">castellated</a> wall surmounts the shield to show the city\'s having been granted status as a <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipality</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">Spanish Crown</a>.\n</p><p>On the flag, the shield sits atop another blue field on which the cross of arrows motif is repeated.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Rail_line_in_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Rail_line_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Rail_line_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="294" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Rail_line_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Rail_line_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Rail_line_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Rail_line_in_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="765" data-file-height="1024" /></a><figcaption>Defunct double gauge rail line of the former railway in Caguas.</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Caguas_trolley.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Caguas_trolley.jpg/180px-Caguas_trolley.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Caguas_trolley.jpg/270px-Caguas_trolley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Caguas_trolley.jpg/360px-Caguas_trolley.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="467" /></a><figcaption>Caguas <a href="/wiki/Tourist_trolley" title="Tourist trolley">Municipal Trolley</a> in the Town Square</figcaption></figure><p>Public transportation in Caguas, as in most of Puerto Rico, is limited to small "guaguas p\xc3\xbablicas" <a href="/wiki/Share_taxi" title="Share taxi">(Mini Bus)</a>. There is inexpensive but slow service to and from <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras, Puerto Rico">Rio Piedras</a>. Several buses and public taxi services serve the town to a limited degree. In 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-Caguas,_PR_&#123;&#123;!&#125;&#125;_Data_USA_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caguas,_PR_{{!}}_Data_USA-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 91.55% of the population relied on their own cars or <a href="/wiki/Carpool" title="Carpool">carpool</a> services to commute.\n</p><p>A "<a href="/wiki/Railcar#Multiple-unit_and_articulated_railcars" title="Railcar">light interurban rail</a>" system connecting <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas_Rail" title="San Juan-Caguas Rail">Caguas to San Juan</a> was in the planning stages and discarded due to lack of funding.\n</p><p>Caguas is served by one freeway, one tolled expressway and one main divided highway. <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_30" title="Puerto Rico Highway 30">Puerto Rico Highway 30</a> connects Caguas to the eastern part of the island. There is no freeway/expressway to the west, due mainly to the fact that there is no sufficient population west of Caguas to develop a new freeway or expressway; good access to the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Cidra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cidra, Puerto Rico">Cidra</a> (southwest) and <a href="/wiki/Aguas_Buenas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguas Buenas, Puerto Rico">Aguas Buenas</a> (northwest) are possible via <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_172" title="Puerto Rico Highway 172">PR-172</a> and <a href="/wiki/PR-156" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-156">PR-156</a>, respectively. <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_52" title="Puerto Rico Highway 52">Puerto Rico Highway 52</a> connects Caguas to the north (<a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>) and south (<a href="/wiki/Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cayey, Puerto Rico">Cayey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>). <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_1" title="Puerto Rico Highway 1">Puerto Rico Highway 1</a> is an alternate route to San Juan and <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a> with two lanes per direction; in south Caguas it becomes rural near <a href="/wiki/Borinquen,_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Borinquen, Caguas, Puerto Rico">Borinquen</a>, therefore the only good access to <a href="/wiki/Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cayey, Puerto Rico">Cayey</a> is the expressway (<a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_52" title="Puerto Rico Highway 52">PR-52</a>) and a $1.00 toll has to be paid (only in the south direction). The only municipality bordering Caguas with a poor-access road is <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Lorenzo, Puerto Rico">San Lorenzo</a>, via <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_183" title="Puerto Rico Highway 183">PR-183</a>; but good access to San Lorenzo is possible by entering <a href="/wiki/Gurabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gurabo, Puerto Rico">Gurabo</a> via <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_30" title="Puerto Rico Highway 30">PR-30</a>, and then taking <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_203" title="Puerto Rico Highway 203">PR-203</a> south. <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport</a> is about 35 minutes away by car.\n</p><p>There are 86 bridges in Caguas.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="High_schools">High schools</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: High schools"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ccnd.org">Colegio Cat\xc3\xb3lico Notre Dame</a></li>\n<li>Elohim Christian Academy</li>\n<li>New Generation Christian Academy (formerly CLA)</li>\n<li>Caguas Military Academy</li>\n<li>Colegio Bautista</li>\n<li>Colegio Cat\xc3\xb3lico San Juan Ap\xc3\xb3stol</li>\n<li>Academia Cristo de los Milagros</li>\n<li>Dr. Juan Jos\xc3\xa9 Osuna High school</li>\n<li>Jos\xc3\xa9 Gautier Ben\xc3\xadtez High school</li>\n<li>Escuela Libre de M\xc3\xbasica - Antonio S. Paoli</li>\n<li>Manuela Toro Morice High School</li>\n<li>Republic of Costa Rica Vocacional High School of Caguas</li>\n<li>Eloisa Pascual "Bairoa III" High School</li>\n<li>Rio Ca\xc3\xb1as High (CIMATEC)</li>\n<li>Caguas Private School (CPS)</li></ul>\n<p>Academia Adventista Caguas\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Higher_education">Higher education</h3><span SANOS</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caguas,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sister cities"><span>edit</span></a><span <a href="/wiki/Hartford,_Connecticut" title="Hartford, Connecticut">Hartford, Connecticut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southbridge,_Massachusetts" title="Southbridge, Massachusetts">Southbridge, Massachusetts</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_People">Notable People</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
